align=\"left\">0.69</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody></table><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/1538-3881/160/5/223/suppdata/ajabb612t2_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-3881/abb612\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/1538-3881/160/5/223/suppdata/ajabb612t2_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>For both models, the majority of GAMA spectroscopy candidates have estimated <em>\u03b8</em><sub>E</sub>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/lesssim.gif\" alt=\"lesssim\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a01'', the GAMA spectroscopy aperture radius. The majority of candidates from the image-based machine-learning and citizen-science methods have a characteristic estimated <em>\u03b8</em><sub>E</sub>\u00a0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/gsim.gif\" alt=\"gsim\" align=\"baseline\" />\u00a01'', mostly above 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />65, the PSF where images of the lens galaxy and arc features can be distinctly separable. We note that some candidates from both GalaxyZoo citizen science and LinKS machine learning have estimated Einstein radii close to or below the PSF, particularly for SIS estimates at low redshift. We have chosen to retain all LinKS candidates as well as those GalaxyZoo candidates with <em>\u03b8</em><sub>E</sub>\u00a0&gt;\u00a00<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />65 in the thin-lens estimate. Because our basic models estimate the Einstein radius with the lens and source positioned along the line of sight, lensing features for a given Einstein radius may in reality extend beyond the estimated Einstein radius due to asymmetry across the line-of-sight axis, allowing for the possibility of detection of lens candidates with Einstein radii smaller than the PSF by image-based techniques.</p><p>Reference <em>\u03b8</em><sub>E</sub> estimates based on SIE models of SLACS (Bolton et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#ajabb612bib11\" id=\"fnref-ajabb612bib11\">2008a</a>), S4TM (Shu et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#ajabb612bib66\" id=\"fnref-ajabb612bib66\">2017</a>), and BELLS (Brownstein et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#ajabb612bib16\" id=\"fnref-ajabb612bib16\">2012</a>; Shu et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#ajabb612bib64\" id=\"fnref-ajabb612bib64\">2016</a>) grade-A lens candidates are shown in the lower plot of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#ajabb612f8\">8</a>. The LinKS machine-learning sample identified candidates with comparable estimated <em>\u03b8</em><sub>E</sub> to the SLACS sample (which was the guide for its training sample), and S4TM and BELLS can be seen to approach the smaller estimated Einstein radii of candidates identified in GAMA spectroscopy. GAMA spectroscopy candidates extend to lower estimated Einstein radii than other spectroscopic selections because GAMA's high completeness reduces mass bias.</p></div><h3 id=\"ajabb612s4-2\" name=\"ajabb612s4-2\">4.2.\u00a0Stellar Mass and Redshift Space</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Analyzing the properties of each catalog in terms of the candidates' stellar mass and redshift, which we illustrate in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#ajabb612f10\">10</a>, we discovered that each method identified galaxies within a distinct region of the parameter space.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"ajabb612f10\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"ajabb612f10\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/160/5/223/Full/ajabb612f10_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 10.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 10.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/160/5/223/Full/ajabb612f10_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 10.</strong>\u00a0Distribution of lens candidates identified by each of the three methods in terms of each candidate's stellar mass and redshift. Histograms above and to the right of the scatter plot indicate the number of candidates identified by each method within specific ranges of stellar mass and redshift, respectively. Each method's catalog occupies a unique range of both characteristics. Left: the two candidates that overlap between GalaxyZoo citizen-science and LinKS machine-learning samples are marked with square and diamond outlines, and we point out candidates G93310 and G136604 that were previously identified in DECaLS (Huang et al. <a class=\"cite\" href=\"#ajabb612bib46\" id=\"fnref-ajabb612bib46\">2020b</a>) and SLACS (Bolton et al. <a class=\"cite\" href=\"#ajabb612bib11\" id=\"fnref-ajabb612bib11\">2008a</a>), respectively. Right: error bars represent uncertainty in stellar mass estimates. Note that 16 GAMA spectroscopy candidates and one LinKS candidate lack reliable stellar mass estimates from the GAMA <span class=\"small-caps\">LAMBDAR</span> catalog and are therefore not shown in the scatter plots.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-ajabb612f10\" href=\"/1538-3881/160/5/223/downloadFigure/figure/ajabb612f10\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-ajabb612f10\" href=\"/1538-3881/160/5/223/downloadHRFigure/figure/ajabb612f10\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>The candidates identified through GAMA spectroscopy tended to be found between <em>z</em>\u00a0~\u00a00.1\u22120.4 (mean 0.250, median 0.253) and with stellar masses between log(<em>M</em><sub>*</sub>/<em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub>)\u00a0~\u00a010.5\u221211.5 (mean 10.98, median 11.18), with a few between log(<em>M</em><sub>*</sub>/<em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub>)\u00a0~ 9.5\u221210.5. For each redshift in the range, there is a characteristic mass we term the <em>fiber radius mass</em> for which the Einstein radius fits in the spectroscopic aperture of the GAMA survey (angular radius = 1''). This is lower than the SDSS fiber radius mass for the same candidate due to a narrower fiber aperture (SDSS fiber aperture is 1<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5). See Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#ajabb612s6-3\">6.3</a>.</p><p>Those candidates identified through LinKS machine learning spanned a slightly higher redshift range (mean 0.316, median 0.322) and tended to be more massive, with the majority of candidates above log(<em>M</em><sub>*</sub>/<em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub>)\u00a0~\u00a011.5 (mean 11.61, median 11.67). As Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#ajabb612f11\">11</a> shows, midrange scoring LinKS candidates can be found throughout the redshift\u2013mass range, with the highest scoring in the high-mass end above log(<em>M</em><sub>*</sub>/<em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub>)\u00a0~\u00a011.5. This is because the training set for the Petrillo et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#ajabb612bib60\" id=\"fnref-ajabb612bib60\">2019a</a>) LinKS machine-learning method is based on intermediate redshift massive galaxies (LRGs) that would have been identified in SDSS spectroscopy, i.e., the SLACS identified sample.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"ajabb612f11\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"ajabb612f11\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/160/5/223/Full/ajabb612f11_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 11.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 11.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/160/5/223/Full/ajabb612f11_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 11.</strong>\u00a0Left: green diamond markers show the stellar mass and redshift of strong lens candidates identified by LinKS machine learning from Petrillo et al. (<a class=\"cite\" href=\"#ajabb612bib60\" id=\"fnref-ajabb612bib60\">2019a</a>). LinKS lens score reflected by the green color bar refers to the authors' visual inspection and scoring of candidates on a scale of 0\u201370, with higher numbers reflecting higher confidence. Mid-scoring objects occur throughout the mass and redshift range, with the highest scoring above log(<em>M</em><sub>*</sub>/<em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub>)\u00a0~\u00a011.5. The highest scoring GalaxyZoo candidates occur in the middle of the stellar mass range of the sample (log(<em>M</em><sub>*</sub>/<em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub>)\u00a0~\u00a011).</p></div><h3 id=\"ajabb612s4-3\" name=\"ajabb612s4-3\">4.3.\u00a0Overlapping Candidates</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The two candidates (G136604 and G124486) common to both LinKS machine learning and GalaxyZoo citizen science fall within the overlap of the parameter space occupied by the two methods' samples in terms of stellar mass and redshift, as shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#ajabb612f10\">10</a>. Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#ajabb612t3\">3</a> compares these two candidates, and their KiDS cutouts are shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#ajabb612f12\">12</a>. Their high scores make these two of the most promising candidates; however, it is worth noting the disagreement between scores given to G136604 by each method. This candidate scored very highly in the LinKS catalog but barely passed GalaxyZoo score selection criteria. G124486 scored around 40% of the maximum possible score for both methods.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"ajabb612f12\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/1538-3881/160/5/223/suppdata/ajabb612t3_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-3881/abb612\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/1538-3881/160/5/223/suppdata/ajabb612t3_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"ajabb612s5\" name=\"ajabb612s5\">5.\u00a0Selection Effects</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>GAMA spectroscopy candidates are selected from a parent subsample of spectroscopic targets in the equatorial regions of GAMA DR3 with spectral template matches of greater than 90% confidence to one of three passive galaxy templates in the <span class=\"small-caps\">autoz</span> algorithm. Stellar masses and redshifts are taken from the GAMA <span class=\"small-caps\">Lambdar</span> catalog, and the resulting sample of 38,278 passive galaxies in GAMA fields G09, G12, and G15 is taken to be the \"parent sample\" for comparison with the GAMA spectroscopy lens candidate sample. Kolmogorov-Smirnov tests between the lens candidate sample and the passive galaxy sample reveal K\u2013S metrics and <em>p</em>-values of 0.0799 and 0.926 in terms of redshift and 0.374 and 4.01\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a010<sup>\u22126</sup> in terms of stellar mass. Note that stellar mass analysis is conducted for only the 31 GAMA spectroscopy candidates with reliable stellar mass estimates. All 47 redshifts are used. This analysis is suggestive (but not significantly, with high <em>p</em>-value) of parity between the parent sample and candidate sample in terms of redshift. The high metric and low <em>p</em>-value for stellar mass indicate a difference between the samples, showing that GAMA spectroscopy does present bias in the mass range of identifiable candidates. Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#ajabb612f13\">13</a> offers a visual description of the distributions of each parameter.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"ajabb612f13\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"ajabb612f13\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/160/5/223/Full/ajabb612f13_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 13.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 13.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/160/5/223/Full/ajabb612f13_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 13.</strong>\u00a0Normalized histograms showing the distributions of the three candidate samples in comparison with their parent samples in terms of redshift and stellar mass. The LinKS machine-learning parent samples include a range of values for an empirical scaling factor that significantly affects the distribution of the parent samples and is shown in the corresponding K\u2013S metrics of Table <a class=\"tabref\" href=\"#ajabb612t4\">4</a>.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-ajabb612f13\" href=\"/1538-3881/160/5/223/downloadFigure/figure/ajabb612f13\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-ajabb612f13\" href=\"/1538-3881/160/5/223/downloadHRFigure/figure/ajabb612f13\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>The LinKS sample (Petrillo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#ajabb612bib60\" id=\"fnref-ajabb612bib60\">2019a</a>) of machine-learning candidates, like its training sample, was selected using color\u2013magnitude cuts modified from the SDSS-LRG (Large Red Galaxy; Eisenstein et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#ajabb612bib34\" id=\"fnref-ajabb612bib34\">2001</a>; Petrillo et al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#ajabb612bib59\" id=\"fnref-ajabb612bib59\">2017</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#ajabb612bib61\" id=\"fnref-ajabb612bib61\">2019b</a>) low-<em>z</em> selection criteria, with magnitudes taken from S-Extractor <span class=\"small-caps\">MagAuto</span>. Additionally, only those objects with effective radii greater than the FWHM of the PSF (times an empirical factor) were selected, in order to remove stellar contaminants. The parent sample for candidates selected within the GAMA equatorial regions therefore includes all galaxies within those regions that satisfy those criteria. Color\u2013magnitude selection includes the following:</p><div xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"display-eqn\" id=\"ajabb612ueqn2\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/160/5/223/Full/ajabb612ueqn2.gif\" alt=\"\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex; mode=display\">\\begin{eqnarray*}&&r\\lt 20\\end{eqnarray*}</script></span></div><p>\n</p><div xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"display-eqn\" id=\"ajabb612ueqn3\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/160/5/223/Full/ajabb612ueqn3.gif\" alt=\"\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex; mode=display\">\\begin{eqnarray*}&&{c}_{\\mathrm{perp}}\\lt 0.2\\end{eqnarray*}</script></span></div><p>\n</p><div xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"display-eqn\" id=\"ajabb612ueqn4\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/160/5/223/Full/ajabb612ueqn4.gif\" alt=\"\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex; mode=display\">\\begin{eqnarray*}&&r\\lt 14+\\displaystyle \\frac{{c}_{\\mathrm{par}}}{0.3}\\end{eqnarray*}</script></span></div><p>where</p><div xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"display-eqn\" id=\"ajabb612ueqn5\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/160/5/223/Full/ajabb612ueqn5.gif\" alt=\"\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex; mode=display\">\\begin{eqnarray*}&&{c}_{\\mathrm{par}}=0.7(g-r)+1.2[(r-i)-0.18)]\\end{eqnarray*}</script></span></div><p>\n</p><div xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"display-eqn\" id=\"ajabb612ueqn6\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/160/5/223/Full/ajabb612ueqn6.gif\" alt=\"\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex; mode=display\">\\begin{eqnarray*}&&{c}_{\\mathrm{perp}}=(r-i)-\\displaystyle \\frac{g-r}{4.0}-0.18.\\end{eqnarray*}</script></span></div><p>We take AB magnitudes from GAMA <span class=\"small-caps\">LAMBDAR</span> SDSS <em>g</em>-, <em>r</em>-, and <em>i</em>-catalogs. Stellar mass and redshift are also taken from GAMA <span class=\"small-caps\">LAMBDAR</span>. Effective radii are taken from single-component S\u00e9rsic fits to the 2D surface brightness distribution in the SDSS <em>r</em>-band from GAMA SersicPhotometry catalog. We select only those objects with effective radii greater than 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />65, the FWHM of the KiDS PSF, times an empirical factor. Because the empirical factor utilized in Petrillo et al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#ajabb612bib59\" id=\"fnref-ajabb612bib59\">2017</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#ajabb612bib60\" id=\"fnref-ajabb612bib60\">2019a</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#ajabb612bib61\" id=\"fnref-ajabb612bib61\">2019b</a>) is not specified, we adopted five values from 1 to 3 to determine the factor's effect on the characteristics of the resulting parent sample selections, the results of which are shown in Table <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#ajabb612t4\">4</a>. The K\u2013S metric for redshift appears to increase monotonically with the increase in this empirical factor, which is also evident in the middle left plot of Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#ajabb612f13\">13</a>. Increasing the value of this empirical factor shifts the distribution of the resulting parent sample to lower redshift. The effect is milder for the stellar mass distribution. The results of these tests indicate to high significance that the LinKS machine-learning sample is not representative of its parent sample for all adopted values of the empirical factor, as it is optimized for identifying high-mass candidates at intermediate redshift.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"ajabb612t4\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/1538-3881/160/5/223/suppdata/ajabb612t4_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-3881/abb612\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/1538-3881/160/5/223/suppdata/ajabb612t4_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>GalaxyZoo selects only objects whose redshift <em>z</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a00.15, so the parent sample for the GalaxyZoo lens candidate sample contains all 40,903 galaxies within the GAMA equatorial fields below that redshift upper limit. Redshifts and stellar masses are taken again from the GAMA <span class=\"small-caps\">LAMBDAR</span> catalog, and K\u2013S tests of redshift and stellar mass yield (K\u2013S metric, <em>p</em>-value) of (0.175, 0.823) and (0.781, 2.55\u00a0<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u00a010<sup>\u22127</sup>), respectively. This indicates a preference for high-mass candidates within its narrow redshift range, which is also indicated in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#ajabb612f13\">13</a>.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"ajabb612t5\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 5.</b>\u00a0\nSLACS Lenses in the GAMA <span computed using the procedure as outlined in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#ajabb612s3-3\">3.3</a>, utilizing the true source redshift as well as adopting the 2:1 ratio assumed for those candidates in this study whose source redshifts are unknown. Here, we present the result of utilizing the true source redshift before the assumed as (true/assumed).</p>\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n\t\t\tDownload table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/1538-3881/160/5/223/suppdata/ajabb612t5_ascii.txt?doi=10.3847/1538-3881/abb612\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/1538-3881/160/5/223/suppdata/ajabb612t5_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>Lensing features become more easily observed in the high-mass range, allowing for easier detectability of objects at higher mass and leading to bias in the candidate population toward these objects by image-based surveys like LinKS and GalaxyZoo, as well as by the inclusion of LRG selection utilized in some mixed spectroscopy efforts. GAMA spectroscopy, which has an upper mass constraint for likelihood of identification at a given redshift if the Einstein radius exceeds the radius of the aperture (see Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#ajabb612s6-3\">6.3</a>), is an exception. GAMA spectroscopy and GalaxyZoo citizen science show little redshift bias from their respective parent sample due to the former's spectroscopic completeness and the latter's narrow redshift range. LinKS machine learning shows a combined redshift and mass difference between the candidate sample and the color\u2013magnitude selected parent sample, suggesting that some bias is instituted after the parent sample selection.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"ajabb612s6\" name=\"ajabb612s6\">6.\u00a0Discussion</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><h3 id=\"ajabb612s6-1\" name=\"ajabb612s6-1\">6.1.\u00a0<em>\u03b8</em><sub>E</sub> Estimates and Empirical Fits</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><h4 id=\"ajabb612s6-1-1\" name=\"ajabb612s6-1-1\">6.1.1.\u00a0Systematic Differences Between Thin-lens and SIS <em>\u03b8</em><sub>E</sub> Estimates</h4><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We further explore the trends introduced in Section <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#ajabb612s4-1\">4.1</a> and Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#ajabb612f9\">9</a> regarding the difference between thin-lens and SIS Einstein radius estimates. In Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#ajabb612f14\">14</a>, we plot the ratio of thin-lens to SIS estimates for each candidate as a function of lens redshift and log(<em>M</em><sub>*</sub>/<em>M</em><sub>\u2299</sub>). In order to understand the relationship between these parameters for LinKS and GalaxyZoo candidates, we set a ratio of Equations (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"eqnref\" href=\"#ajabb612eqn1\">1</a>) and (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"eqnref\" href=\"#ajabb612eqn3\">3</a>)</p><div xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"display-eqn\" id=\"ajabb612eqn6\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/160/5/223/Full/ajabb612eqn6.gif\" alt=\"Equation (6)\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex; mode=display\">\\begin{eqnarray}&&\\displaystyle \\frac{{\\theta }_{{\\rm{E}},\\mathrm{TL}}}{{\\theta }_{{\\rm{E}},\\mathrm{SIS}}}={\\left(\\displaystyle \\frac{4{{GM}}_{{\\rm{E}}}{D}_{{LS}}}{{c}^{2}{D}_{S}{D}_{L}}\\right)}^{1/2}\\left(\\displaystyle \\frac{{D}_{S}{c}^{2}}{4\\pi {\\sigma }_{\\mathrm{SIS}}^{2}{D}_{{LS}}}\\right)\\end{eqnarray}\n\t\t\t\t\\tag{\n\t\t\t\t6\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t</script></span></div><p>\n</p><div xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"display-eqn\" id=\"ajabb612eqn7\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/160/5/223/Full/ajabb612eqn7.gif\" alt=\"Equation (7)\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex; mode=display\">\\begin{eqnarray}&&=\\ \\left(\\displaystyle \\frac{{G}^{1/2}c}{2\\pi }\\right)\\left(\\displaystyle \\frac{{M}_{{\\rm{E}}}^{1/2}}{{\\sigma }_{\\mathrm{SIS}}^{2}}\\right){\\left(\\displaystyle \\frac{{D}_{S}}{{D}_{L}{D}_{{LS}}}\\right)}^{1/2}\\end{eqnarray}\n\t\t\t\t\\tag{\n\t\t\t\t7\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t</script></span></div><p>\n</p><div xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"display-eqn\" id=\"ajabb612eqn8\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/160/5/223/Full/ajabb612eqn8.gif\" alt=\"Equation (8)\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex; mode=display\">\\begin{eqnarray}&&=\\ \\beta {\\left(\\displaystyle \\frac{{M}_{* }}{{M}_{\\odot }}\\right)}^{{\\rm{\\Gamma }}}{\\left(\\displaystyle \\frac{{D}_{S}}{{D}_{{LS}}}\\right)}^{1/2}{\\left(\\displaystyle \\frac{1}{{D}_{L}}\\right)}^{1/2}\\end{eqnarray}\n\t\t\t\t\\tag{\n\t\t\t\t8\n\t\t\t\t}\n\t\t\t</script></span></div><p>where Equation (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"eqnref\" href=\"#ajabb612eqn8\">8</a>) substitutes Equations (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"eqnref\" href=\"#ajabb612eqn2\">2</a>), (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"eqnref\" href=\"#ajabb612eqn4\">4</a>), and (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"eqnref\" href=\"#ajabb612eqn5\">5</a>) for the values of <em>M</em><sub>E</sub> and <em>\u03c3</em><sub>SIS</sub> in Equation (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"eqnref\" href=\"#ajabb612eqn7\">7</a>), and</p><div xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"display-eqn\" id=\"ajabb612ueqn7\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/160/5/223/Full/ajabb612ueqn7.gif\" alt=\"\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex; mode=display\">\\begin{eqnarray*}&&\\begin{array}{l}\\beta ={\\left(1.90\\times {10}^{6}{\\rm{Mpc}}\\right)}^{1/2},\\quad {\\rm{\\Gamma }}=-0.181\\\\ {\\rm{for}}\\qquad z\\lt 0.2,\\qquad {M}_{* }\\leqslant {M}_{b}\\\\ \\beta ={\\left(57.4{\\rm{Mpc}}\\right)}^{1/2},\\quad {\\rm{\\Gamma }}=0.039\\qquad \\\\ {\\rm{for}}\\qquad z\\lt 0.2,\\qquad {M}_{* }\\gt {M}_{b}\\\\ \\beta ={\\left(19.1{\\rm{Mpc}}\\right)}^{1/2},\\quad {\\rm{\\Gamma }}=0.063\\qquad \\\\ {\\rm{for}}\\qquad 0.2\\ z\\lt 0.65.\\end{array}\\end{eqnarray*}</script></span></div><p>\n</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"ajabb612f14\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"ajabb612f14\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/160/5/223/Full/ajabb612f14_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 14.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 14.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/160/5/223/Full/ajabb612f14_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 14.</strong>\u00a0The ratio between thin-lens and SIS estimates of Einstein radius as a function of two parameters, lens redshift and lens stellar mass. The black surface indicates the relationship between these parameters when assuming the simplifying 2:1 ratio of source distance to lens distance. All LinKS machine-learning and GalaxyZoo citizen-science candidates are intersected by this surface. The surface is defined by three distinct piecewise regions as a result of the different velocity dispersion estimates adopted from Zahid et al. (<a class=\"cite\" href=\"#ajabb612bib81\" id=\"fnref-ajabb612bib81\">2016</a>) and described in Section <a class=\"secref\" href=\"#ajabb612s3-3\">3.3</a>.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-ajabb612f14\" href=\"/1538-3881/160/5/223/downloadFigure/figure/ajabb612f14\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-ajabb612f14\" href=\"/1538-3881/160/5/223/downloadHRFigure/figure/ajabb612f14\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>We assume the source distance to be twice the lens distance, so the middle parentheses term of Equation (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"eqnref\" href=\"#ajabb612eqn8\">8</a>) becomes <span xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"inline-eqn\"><span class=\"tex\"><span class=\"texImage\"><img src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/1538-3881/160/5/223/Full/ajabb612ieqn4.gif\" alt=\"$\\sqrt{2}$\" align=\"top\"></img></span><script type=\"math/tex\">\\sqrt{2}</script></span></span>, and the resulting function describes a surface in this three-dimensional parameter space that intersects each point representing the LinKS and GalaxyZoo candidates, as shown in Figure <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#ajabb612f14\">14</a>. This function shows a clear dependence of the value of this ratio on the inverse square root of the lens distance. This dependence holds for each of the three distinct conditional regions of redshift and stellar mass described in Equations (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"eqnref\" href=\"#ajabb612eqn4\">4</a>) and (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"eqnref\" href=\"#ajabb612eqn5\">5</a>). This shows a pronounced difference between the estimates for these candidates at lower redshift. There is a strong correlation between mass and redshift for these candidates, where stellar mass increases with redshift. All LinKS and GalaxyZoo candidates lie in the region above <em>M</em><sub>*</sub>\u00a0=\u00a0<em>M</em><sub><em>b</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a010<sup>10.26</sup>, where this ratio value decreases with decreasing stellar mass. Therefore, the observed trend of a greater difference in <em>\u03b8</em><sub>E</sub> estimates for candidates at lower redshift does not appear to be due to a mass dependence, which is in fact a competing dependence.</p><div tabindex=\"-1\" id=\"ajabb612t6\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\"><p><b>Table 6.</b>\u00a0\nStrong Lenses With Archival Hubble Data Available from the Hubble Legacy Archive\n</p><table cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" border=\"0\" data-toolbar-link=\"ajabb612t6\" data-toolbar-img=\"/1538-3881/160/5/223/suppdata/ajabb612t6_lr.gif\" data-toolbar-type=\"table\" data-toolbar-title=\"Table 6\"><colgroup><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col><col align=\"left\"></col></colgroup><thead>\n<tr
